   888	
   889	    [Fact]
   890	    public void Key_Enter_Activates_And_Accepts_Focused_Item ()
   891	    {
   892	        // Arrange
   893	        OptionSelector optionSelector = new ();
   894	        optionSelector.Labels = ["Option1", "Option2", "Option3"];
   895	        optionSelector.Value = 0;
   896	        optionSelector.SetFocus ();
   897	        optionSelector.Layout ();
   898	
   899	        // Focus the second item (which is NOT the active/selected item)
   900	        CheckBox [] checkBoxes = optionSelector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox> ().ToArray ();
   901	        checkBoxes [1].SetFocus ();
   902	        Assert.True (checkBoxes [1].HasFocus);
   903	        Assert.Equal (0, optionSelector.Value); // Option1 is still selected
   904	
   905	        var activatingCount = 0;
   906	        optionSelector.Activating += (_, _) => activatingCount++;
   907	
   908	        var acceptingCount = 0;
   909	        optionSelector.Accepting += (_, _) => acceptingCount++;
   910	
   911	        var valueChangedCount = 0;
   912	        optionSelector.ValueChanged += (_, _) => valueChangedCount++;
   913	
   914	        // Act - Press Enter on the focused (but not selected) checkbox
   915	        checkBoxes [1].NewKeyDownEvent (Key.Enter);
   916	
   917	        // Assert - Per spec: Enter should Activate AND Accept
   918	        Assert.Equal (1, activatingCount);
   919	        Assert.Equal (1, acceptingCount);
   920	        Assert.Equal (1, valueChangedCount);
   921	        Assert.Equal (1, optionSelector.Value); // Should now be Option2
   922	    }
   923	
   924	    [Fact]
   925	    public void Key_Enter_On_Active_Item_Accepts ()
   926	    {
   927	        // Arrange
   928	        OptionSelector optionSelector = new ();
   929	        optionSelector.Labels = ["Option1", "Option2", "Option3"];
   930	        optionSelector.Value = 0;
   931	        optionSelector.SetFocus ();
   932	        optionSelector.Layout ();
   933	
   934	        // Focus the first item (which IS the active/selected item)
   935	        CheckBox [] checkBoxes = optionSelector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox> ().ToArray ();
   936	        checkBoxes [0].SetFocus ();
   937	        Assert.True (checkBoxes [0].HasFocus);
   938	        Assert.Equal (0, optionSelector.Value); // Option1 is still selected
   939	
   940	        var activatingCount = 0;
   941	        optionSelector.Activating += (_, _) => activatingCount++;
   942	
   943	        var acceptingCount = 0;
   944	        optionSelector.Accepting += (_, _) => acceptingCount++;
   945	
   946	        var valueChangedCount = 0;
   947	        optionSelector.ValueChanged += (_, _) => valueChangedCount++;
   948	
   949	        // Act - Press Enter on the focused (but not selected) checkbox
   950	        checkBoxes [0].NewKeyDownEvent (Key.Enter);
   951	
   952	        // Assert - Per spec: Enter should Activate AND Accept
   953	        Assert.Equal (1, activatingCount);
   954	        Assert.Equal (1, acceptingCount);
   955	        Assert.Equal (0, valueChangedCount);
   956	        Assert.Equal (0, optionSelector.Value); // Should be Option1
   957	        Assert.True (optionSelector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox> ().Count (cb => cb.Value == CheckState.Checked) == 1);
   958	    }
   959	
   960	    #region Value Propagation via Activated Event (CWP Bug Tests)
   961	
   962	    // Claude - Sonnet 4.6
   963	    /// <summary>
   964	    ///     Proves the CWP ordering bug: <see cref="OptionSelector.OnActivated"/> calls
   965	    ///     <c>base.OnActivated</c> (which fires <see cref="View.Activated"/>) BEFORE
   966	    ///     <c>ApplyActivation</c> updates <see cref="SelectorBase.Value"/>.
   967	    ///     The <see cref="ICommandContext.Value"/> carried by <see cref="View.Activated"/> must be
   968	    ///     the <see cref="OptionSelector"/>'s semantic <see cref="int"/>? index,
   969	    ///     not the dispatched <see cref="CheckBox"/>'s <see cref="CheckState"/>.
   970	    /// </summary>
   971	    [Fact]
   972	    public void Activated_Event_Value_Is_OptionSelector_Int_Not_CheckState ()
   973	    {
   974	        // Arrange: OptionSelector with two options; second option focused for dispatch.
   975	        OptionSelector optionSelector = new ();
   976	        optionSelector.Labels = ["Option1", "Option2"];
   977	        optionSelector.SetFocus ();
   978	        optionSelector.Layout ();
   979	
   980	        Assert.Equal (0, optionSelector.Value); // Option1 selected
   981	
   982	        // Focus Option2 so InvokeCommand dispatches Activate to it.
   983	        CheckBox option2 = optionSelector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox> ().First (cb => cb.Title == "Option2");
   984	        option2.SetFocus ();
   985	
   986	        object capturedValue = null;
   987	        int activatedCount = 0;
   988	
   989	        optionSelector.Activated += (_, args) =>
   990	        {
   991	            activatedCount++;
   992	            capturedValue = args.Value?.Value;
   993	        };
   994	
   995	        // Act: Activate on the selector dispatches down to the focused CheckBox (Option2).
   996	        optionSelector.InvokeCommand (Command.Activate);
   997	
   998	        // Assert: OptionSelector.Value changed to 1 (Option2 selected).
   999	        Assert.Equal (1, optionSelector.Value);
  1000	        Assert.Equal (1, activatedCount);
  1001	
  1002	        // The value arriving at Activated must be the OptionSelector's int? (1),
  1003	        // NOT the dispatched CheckBox's CheckState (CheckState.Checked).
  1004	        Assert.Null (capturedValue as CheckState?);    // Must NOT be a CheckState
  1005	        Assert.Equal ((int?)1, capturedValue as int?); // Must be the OptionSelector's index
  1006	
  1007	        optionSelector.Dispose ();
  1008	    }
  1009	
  1010	    // Claude - Sonnet 4.6
  1011	    /// <summary>
  1012	    ///     Proves that an ancestor subscribing to <see cref="View.Activated"/> via
  1013	    ///     <see cref="View.CommandsToBubbleUp"/> receives the <see cref="OptionSelector"/>'s
  1014	    ///     semantic <see cref="int"/>? value — not the inner <see cref="CheckBox"/>'s
  1015	    ///     <see cref="CheckState"/> — through the <c>BubbleActivatedUp</c> path.
  1016	    ///     Uses <see cref="Application"/> context so focus propagates correctly through
  1017	    ///     the hierarchy and the dispatch goes to the focused CheckBox, not the Cycle path.
  1018	    /// </summary>
  1019	    [Fact]
  1020	    public void Activated_Event_Ancestor_Receives_OptionSelector_Value_Via_BubbleActivatedUp ()
  1021	    {
  1022	        // Arrange: Application context ensures SetFocus works through nested hierarchy.
  1023	        VirtualTimeProvider time = new ();
  1024	
  1025	        using IApplication app = Application.Create (time);
  1026	        app.Init (DriverRegistry.Names.ANSI);
  1027	        IRunnable runnable = new Runnable ();
  1028	
  1029	        // ancestor opts in to Activate bubbling and contains the OptionSelector.
  1030	        // CanFocus = true is required so the focus chain can propagate through ancestor.
  1031	        View ancestor = new () { Id = "ancestor", CanFocus = true };
  1032	        ancestor.CommandsToBubbleUp = [Command.Activate];
  1033	
  1034	        OptionSelector optionSelector = new ();
  1035	        optionSelector.Labels = ["Option1", "Option2"];
  1036	        ancestor.Add (optionSelector);
  1037	
  1038	        (runnable as View)!.Add (ancestor);
  1039	        app.Begin (runnable);
  1040	
  1041	        Assert.Equal (0, optionSelector.Value); // Option1 selected
  1042	
  1043	        // Focus Option2 so Activate dispatches to it.
  1044	        CheckBox option2 = optionSelector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox> ().First (cb => cb.Title == "Option2");
  1045	        option2.HasFocus = true;
  1046	        Assert.True (option2.HasFocus);
  1047	
  1048	        object capturedValue = null;
  1049	        int ancestorActivatedCount = 0;
  1050	
  1051	        ancestor.Activated += (_, args) =>
  1052	        {
  1053	            ancestorActivatedCount++;
  1054	            capturedValue = args.Value?.Value;
  1055	        };
  1056	
  1057	        // Act: Activate dispatches down to Option2, then BubbleActivatedUp reaches ancestor.
  1058	        optionSelector.InvokeCommand (Command.Activate);
  1059	
  1060	        // Assert: OptionSelector.Value changed; ancestor received Activated exactly once.
  1061	        Assert.Equal (1, optionSelector.Value);
  1062	        Assert.Equal (1, ancestorActivatedCount);
  1063	
  1064	        // The ancestor must receive the OptionSelector's int? (1), NOT a CheckState.
  1065	        Assert.Null (capturedValue as CheckState?);    // Must NOT be a CheckState
  1066	        Assert.Equal ((int?)1, capturedValue as int?); // Must be the OptionSelector's index
  1067	
  1068	        ancestor.Dispose ();
  1069	    }
  1070	
  1071	    #endregion

   480	    [Fact]
   481	    public void DoubleClickAccepts_True_AcceptOnDoubleClick ()
   482	    {
   483	        // Arrange
   484	        VirtualTimeProvider time = new ();
   485	        using IApplication app = Application.Create (time);
   486	        app.Init (DriverRegistry.Names.ANSI);
   487	        IRunnable runnable = new Runnable ();
   488	
   489	        var selector = new OptionSelector { DoubleClickAccepts = true };
   490	        selector.Labels = ["Option1", "Option2"];
   491	
   492	        (runnable as View)?.Add (selector);
   493	        app.Begin (runnable);
   494	
   495	        var acceptCount = 0;
   496	        selector.Accepting += (_, _) => acceptCount++;
   497	
   498	        CheckBox checkBox = selector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox> ().First ();
   499	        app.InjectSequence (InputInjectionExtensions.LeftButtonDoubleClick (checkBox.Frame.Location));
   500	
   501	        Assert.Equal (1, acceptCount);
   502	        Assert.Equal (0, selector.Value); // Should select the first option on double-click
   503	
   504	        checkBox = selector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox> ().Last ();
   505	        app.InjectSequence (InputInjectionExtensions.LeftButtonDoubleClick (checkBox.Frame.Location));
   506	
   507	        Assert.Equal (2, acceptCount);
   508	        Assert.Equal (1, selector.Value); // Should select the 2nd option on double-click
   509	    }
   510	
   511	    [Fact]
   512	    public void DoubleClickAccepts_False_DoesNotAcceptOnDoubleClick ()
   513	    {
   514	        // Arrange
   515	        VirtualTimeProvider time = new ();

   518	        IRunnable runnable = new Runnable ();

   563	    {
   564	        OptionSelector selector = new ();
   565	
   566	        selector.Labels = ["Test Option"];
   567	        selector.Values = [42];
   568	
   569	        CheckBox checkBox = selector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox> ().First ();
   570	        Assert.Equal ("Test Option", checkBox.Title);
   571	        Assert.Equal ("Test Option", checkBox.Id);
   572	        Assert.Equal (42, selector.GetCheckBoxValue (checkBox));
   573	        Assert.True (checkBox.CanFocus);
   574	    }
   575	
   576	    #endregion
   577	
   578	    #region HotKey Command Tests
   579	
   580	    [Fact]
   581	    public void HotKey_Command_DoesNotFireAccept ()
   582	    {
   583	        OptionSelector selector = new ();
   584	        selector.Labels = ["Option1", "Option2"];
   585	
   586	        var acceptCount = 0;
   587	        selector.Accepting += (_, _) => acceptCount++;
   588	
   589	        selector.InvokeCommand (Command.HotKey);
   590	
   591	        Assert.Equal (0, acceptCount);
   592	    }
   593	
   594	    [Fact]
   595	    public void Accept_Command_FiresAccept ()
   596	    {
   597	        OptionSelector selector = new ();
   598	        selector.Labels = ["Option1", "Option2"];
   599	
   600	        var acceptCount = 0;
   601	        selector.Accepting += (_, _) => acceptCount++;
   602	
   603	        selector.InvokeCommand (Command.Accept);
   604	
   605	        Assert.Equal (1, acceptCount);
   606	    }
   607	
   608	    #endregion
   609	
   610	    #region Edge Cases
   611	
   612	    [Fact]
   613	    public void EmptyLabels_CreatesNoSubViews ()
   614	    {
   615	        OptionSelector selector = new ();
   616	
   617	        selector.Labels = [];
   618	
   619	        Assert.Empty (selector.SubViews);
   620	    }
   621	
   622	    [Fact]
   623	    public void Value_WithNoLabels_CanBeSet ()
   624	    {
   625	        OptionSelector selector = new ();
   626	
   627	        // This should work even without labels
   628	        Exception? exception = Record.Exception (() => selector.Value = null);
   629	
   630	        Assert.Null (exception);
   631	        Assert.Null (selector.Value);
   632	    }
   633	
   634	    #endregion
   635	
   636	    #region Navigation Keys
   637	
   638	    [Theory]
   639	    [InlineData (SelectorStyles.None)]
   640	    [InlineData (SelectorStyles.ShowNoneFlag)]
   641	    [InlineData (SelectorStyles.ShowAllFlag)]
   642	    [InlineData (SelectorStyles.ShowValue)]
   643	    [InlineData (SelectorStyles.All)]
   644	    public void Navigation_Keys_Move_Out_And_Into_Not_Within (SelectorStyles selectorStyles)
   645	    {
   646	        using IApplication app = Application.Create ().Init (DriverRegistry.Names.ANSI);
   647	        using Runnable runnable = new ();
   648	        var view1 = new View { CanFocus = true };
   649	
   650	        OptionSelector selector = new ()
   651	        {
   652	            Styles = selectorStyles,
   653	            TabBehavior = TabBehavior.NoStop
   654	        };
   655	        List<string> options = ["Option1", "Option2", "Option3"];
   656	        selector.Labels = options;
   657	        var view2 = new View { CanFocus = true };
   658	        runnable.Add (view1, selector, view2);
   659	
   660	        app.Begin (runnable);
   661	
   662	        // Set focus to view1
   663	        view1.SetFocus ();
   664	
   665	        // Invoke Tab command to move focus to selector
   666	        Assert.True (app.Keyboard.RaiseKeyDownEvent (Key.Tab));
   667	        Assert.True (selector.HasFocus);
   668	
   669	        // Invoke Tab command again to move focus to view2
   670	        Assert.True (app.Keyboard.RaiseKeyDownEvent (Key.Tab));
   671	        Assert.True (view2.HasFocus);
   672	
   673	        // Now test Shift+Tab to move focus back to selector
   674	        Assert.True (app.Keyboard.RaiseKeyDownEvent (Key.Tab.WithShift));
   675	        Assert.True (selector.HasFocus);
   676	
   677	        // Finally, Shift+Tab again to move focus back to view1
   678	        Assert.True (app.Keyboard.RaiseKeyDownEvent (Key.Tab.WithShift));
   679	        Assert.True (view1.HasFocus);
   680	    }
   681	
   682	    #endregion
   683	}

2026-05-29 16:37:19,208 - INFO - swea-agent-gui-cs__Terminal.Gui-4860 - 💭 THOUGHT
Let me look at the code more carefully. The key insight is in `CreateSubViews()`. After it removes all views and adds new ones, `Add` calls `SetNeedsLayout()`. But `SetLayout()` is also called which modifies the subviews' dimensions. The issue might be that `SetLayout()` sets `Width = Dim.Auto()` on subviews, which changes their width dimension, but this doesn't trigger `SetNeedsLayout()` on the parent again.

Actually, let me re-read the `Labels` setter and `Values` setter again:

```csharp
public IReadOnlyList<string>? Labels
{
    get;
    set
    {
        field = value;
        CreateSubViews ();
        UpdateChecked ();
    }
}

public virtual IReadOnlyList<int>? Values
{
    get { ... }
    set
    {
        field = value;
        if (Value is null && field?.Any () == true)
        {
            Value = field.First ();
        }
        CreateSubViews ();
        UpdateChecked ();
    }
}
```

When Labels is set:
1. `field = value` (sets backing field)
2. `CreateSubViews()` - if Values is null, this returns early
3. `UpdateChecked()` - no-op since no subviews

When Values is set:
1. `field = value`
2. If Value is null, set to first value
3. `CreateSubViews()` - now both Labels and Values are set, so subviews are created
4. `UpdateChecked()`

In `CreateSubViews()`:
1. `RemoveAll()` - triggers `SetNeedsLayout()` on parent
2. For each label, `Add(CreateCheckBox(...))` - triggers `SetNeedsLayout()` on parent
3. `SetLayout()` - sets subview X, Y, Width, but does NOT trigger `SetNeedsLayout()` on parent

So after `CreateSubViews()`, the parent has `SetNeedsLayout()` called multiple times. When layout runs, it should compute the correct size.

But wait - the issue says "Setting `Labels` and `Values` after construction doesn't trigger a width recalculation." Maybe the problem is that when the view is not yet part of a visible hierarchy, `SetNeedsLayout()` marks it, but the layout doesn't actually run until the view is added to a running application. At that point, the layout should compute correctly...

Let me look at the `DimAuto.Calculate` method more carefully, specifically how `PosAlign` subviews are handled:

In `DimAuto.Calculate` for `DimAutoStyle.Content`:
- Views are categorized
- For not-dependent views: `notDependentSubView.SetRelativeLayout(us.GetContentSize())` is called, then size is calculated
- For PosView, DimView, DimAuto based views: `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` is called

The `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` method:
```csharp
private static int CalculateMaxSizeFromList (List<View> views, int max, Dimension dimension)
{
    foreach (View v in views)
    {
        int newMax = dimension == Dimension.Width
                         ? v.Frame.X + v.Width.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension)
                         : v.Frame.Y + v.Height.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension);
        if (newMax > max)
        {
            max = newMax;
        }
    }
    return max;
}
```

For the horizontal case with `PosAlign`:
- Subviews have `X = Pos.Align(...)` and `Width = Dim.Auto()`
- When calculating width:
  - `v.Frame.X` is the current X position (which is 0 before layout)
  - `v.Width.Calculate(0, max, v, dimension)` computes the auto width

But `v.Frame.X` might be 0 initially, and the width calculation should give us the right size. Let me think about this differently.

Actually, I think the problem might be more specific. Let me look at how `PosAlign` interacts with the auto-size calculation. In `CategorizeViews`:

```csharp
if (pos.Has<PosAlign> (out _))
{
    categories.AlignGroupIds.Add (posAlign.GroupId);
}
```

`PosAlign` views are categorized under `AlignGroupIds`. Then later:
```csharp
// Process aligned views
var maxAlign = 0;
foreach (int groupId in categories.AlignGroupIds)
{
    maxAlign = PosAlign.CalculateMinDimension (groupId, us.InternalSubViews.ToArray (), dimension);
}
maxCalculatedSize = int.Max (maxCalculatedSize, maxAlign);
```

And `CalculateMinDimension`:
```csharp
public static int CalculateMinDimension (int groupId, IReadOnlyCollection<View> views, Dimension dimension)
{
    var dimensionsSum = 0;
    foreach (View view in views)
    {
        if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            continue;

        PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;
        if (posAlign is { })
        {
            dimensionsSum += dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.Frame.Width : view.Frame.Height;
        }
    }
    return dimensionsSum;
}
```

This sums up the `Frame.Width` of all views with `PosAlign`. But `Frame.Width` is the current frame width, which may not have been calculated yet! The `SetRelativeLayout` hasn't been called for these views before `CalculateMinDimension` is called. So `Frame.Width` might be 0.

Wait, let me look again at `Calculate`:

```csharp
// Process not-dependent views
foreach (View notDependentSubView in categories.NotDependent)
{
    notDependentSubView.SetRelativeLayout (us.GetContentSize ());
    ...
}

// Process centered views
...

// Process aligned views
var maxAlign = 0;
foreach (int groupId in categories.AlignGroupIds)
{
    maxAlign = PosAlign.CalculateMinDimension (groupId, us.InternalSubViews.ToArray (), dimension);
}
```

For not-dependent views, `SetRelativeLayout` is called first. But for aligned views (PosAlign), `SetRelativeLayout` is NOT called before `CalculateMinDimension`. So `Frame.Width` may be 0.

But wait, the checkboxes in horizontal mode have both `PosAlign` (X) and `DimAuto` (Width). In `CategorizeViews`, a view can be in multiple categories. So a checkbox with `X = PosAlign` and `Width = DimAuto` would be in:
- `NotDependent` - if pos.IsFixed || dim.IsFixed (PosAlign is NOT fixed, DimAuto IS fixed)
- Wait, `DimAuto.IsFixed` returns `true` (line 39 in DimAuto.cs). And `PosAlign.IsFixed`? Let me check.

Actually, `NotDependent` checks:
```csharp
if ((pos.IsFixed || dim.IsFixed) && !pos.DependsOnSuperViewContentSize && !dim.DependsOnSuperViewContentSize)
```

`DimAuto.IsFixed` = true (from DimAuto.cs line 39). But `PosAlign.DependsOnSuperViewContentSize` = true (from PosAlign.cs line 179). So the condition `!pos.DependsOnSuperViewContentSize` is false, meaning the view is NOT added to `NotDependent`. Good.

So the checkbox with `PosAlign` X and `DimAuto` Width ends up in:
- `DimAutoBased` (DimAuto width)
- `AlignGroupIds` (PosAlign X)

Now, in `Calculate`:
1. First `NotDependent` is processed (our checkboxes are NOT here)
2. `Centered` (not here)
3. `AlignGroupIds` - `CalculateMinDimension` is called which sums `Frame.Width` of the views
4. `PosViewBased`, `DimViewBased`, `DimAutoBased` - `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` is called

The problem: when processing `AlignGroupIds`, `CalculateMinDimension` sums `view.Frame.Width`. But `Frame.Width` hasn't been computed yet because `SetRelativeLayout` hasn't been called for these views. The `DimAutoBased` processing happens AFTER `AlignGroupIds`, but the damage is done - the aligned views' `Frame.Width` is 0 at that point.

Actually wait, let me re-read the code more carefully. The views are in multiple categories. Let me trace through the exact flow:

For each checkbox in horizontal mode:
- `X = PosAlign(Alignment.Start, AlignmentModes.StartToEnd)` 
- `Width = DimAuto()`

Categorization:
- `NotDependent`: checks `(pos.IsFixed || dim.IsFixed) && !pos.DependsOnSuperViewContentSize && !dim.DependsOnSuperViewContentSize`. `DimAuto.IsFixed` = true, `PosAlign.IsFixed` - probably false. But `PosAlign.DependsOnSuperViewContentSize` = true, so fails. Not in `NotDependent`.
- `Centered`: `pos.Has<PosCenter>` - no
- `Anchored`: `pos.Has<PosAnchorEnd>` - no  
- `PosViewBased`: `pos.Has<PosView>` - no
- `DimViewBased`: `dim.Has<DimView>` - no (it's DimAuto)
- `DimAutoBased`: `dim.Has<DimAuto>` - YES
- `DimFillBased`: no
- `AlignGroupIds`: `pos.Has(out PosAlign posAlign)` - YES

So each checkbox ends up in both `DimAutoBased` and `AlignGroupIds`.

Now in `Calculate`:
1. Process `NotDependent` - nothing
2. Process `Centered` - nothing
3. Process `AlignGroupIds` - calls `CalculateMinDimension` which sums `view.Frame.Width`. At this point, `Frame.Width` is 0 because no layout has been done yet. So `maxAlign` = 0.
4. Process `AnchorEnd` - nothing
5. Process `PosViewBased`, `DimViewBased`, `DimAutoBased` via `CalculateMaxSizeFromList`:
   ```csharp
   int newMax = dimension == Dimension.Width
                    ? v.Frame.X + v.Width.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension)
                    : ...
   ```
   `v.Frame.X` is still 0 (PosAlign hasn't been calculated). `v.Width.Calculate(0, max, v, dimension)` - this calculates the auto width of the checkbox. For a checkbox with `DimAuto(DimAutoStyle.Text)`, this would calculate the text width.

So we get the right width for each checkbox individually, but `Frame.X` is 0, so the total `maxCalculatedSize` becomes just the width of one checkbox (the widest one). The parent's width becomes the width of the widest checkbox, not the sum of all checkboxes.

THIS is the bug! The horizontal layout uses `Pos.Align` which distributes the checkboxes horizontally, but the auto-size calculation doesn't account for the fact that PosAlign distributes views across the available space. The `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` just uses `Frame.X + Width`, where `Frame.X` is 0.

Wait, but `PosAlign.Calculate` is supposed to compute the X positions. Let me look at `PosAlign.Calculate`:

```csharp
internal override int Calculate (int superviewDimension, Dim dim, View us, Dimension dimension)
{
    if (_cachedLocation.HasValue && Aligner.ContainerSize == superviewDimension && !us.NeedsLayout)
    {
        return _cachedLocation.Value;
    }

    List<View> groupViews = us.SuperView is null ? [us] : us.SuperView!.SubViews.Snapshot ().Where (v => HasGroupId (v, dimension, GroupId)).ToList ();
    AlignAndUpdateGroup (GroupId, groupViews, dimension, superviewDimension);
    ...
}
```

This calls `AlignAndUpdateGroup` which calculates positions and caches them. But the positions are calculated based on the `Aligner` container size.

    59	    public event PropertyChangedEventHandler PropertyChanged;
    60	
    61	    /// <summary>
    62	    ///     Takes a list of item sizes and returns a list of the positions of those items when aligned within
    63	    ///     <see name="ContainerSize"/>
    64	    ///     using the <see cref="Alignment"/> and <see cref="AlignmentModes"/> settings.
    65	    /// </summary>
    66	    /// <param name="sizes">The sizes of the items to align.</param>
    67	    /// <returns>The locations of the items, from left/top to right/bottom.</returns>
    68	    public int [] Align (int [] sizes) => Align (Alignment, AlignmentModes, ContainerSize, sizes);
    69	
    70	    /// <summary>
    71	    ///     Takes a list of item sizes and returns a list of the  positions of those items when aligned within
    72	    ///     <paramref name="containerSize"/>
    73	    ///     using specified parameters.
    74	    /// </summary>
    75	    /// <param name="alignment">Specifies how the items will be aligned.</param>
    76	    /// <param name="alignmentMode"></param>
    77	    /// <param name="containerSize">The size of the container.</param>
    78	    /// <param name="sizes">The sizes of the items to align.</param>
    79	    /// <returns>The positions of the items, from left/top to right/bottom.</returns>
    80	    public static int [] Align (in Alignment alignment, in AlignmentModes alignmentMode, in int containerSize, in int [] sizes)
    81	    {
    82	        if (sizes.Length == 0)
    83	        {
    84	            return [];
    85	        }
    86	
    87	        int [] sizesCopy = sizes;
    88	
    89	        if (alignmentMode.FastHasFlags (AlignmentModes.EndToStart))
    90	        {
    91	            sizesCopy = sizes.Reverse ().ToArray ();
    92	        }
    93	
    94	        int maxSpaceBetweenItems = alignmentMode.FastHasFlags (AlignmentModes.AddSpaceBetweenItems) ? 1 : 0;
    95	        int totalItemsSize = sizes.Sum ();
    96	        int totalGaps = sizes.Length - 1; // total gaps between items
    97	        int totalItemsAndSpaces = totalItemsSize + totalGaps * maxSpaceBetweenItems; // total size of items and spacesToGive if we had enough room
    98	        int spacesToGive = totalGaps * maxSpaceBetweenItems; // We'll decrement this below to place one space between each item until we run out
    99	
   100	        if (totalItemsSize >= containerSize)
   101	        {
   102	            spacesToGive = 0;
   103	        }
   104	        else if (totalItemsAndSpaces > containerSize)
   105	        {
   106	            spacesToGive = containerSize - totalItemsSize;
   107	        }
   108	
   109	        AlignmentModes mode = alignmentMode & ~AlignmentModes.AddSpaceBetweenItems; // copy to avoid modifying the original
   110	
   111	        switch (alignment)
   112	        {
   113	            case Alignment.Start:
   114	                switch (mode)
   115	                {
   116	                    case AlignmentModes.StartToEnd:
   117	                        return Start (in sizesCopy, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive);
   118	
   119	                    case AlignmentModes.StartToEnd | AlignmentModes.IgnoreFirstOrLast:
   120	                        return IgnoreLast (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive);
   121	
   122	                    case AlignmentModes.EndToStart:
   123	                        return End (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive).Reverse ().ToArray ();
   124	
   125	                    case AlignmentModes.EndToStart | AlignmentModes.IgnoreFirstOrLast:
   126	                        return IgnoreFirst (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive).Reverse ().ToArray ();
   127	                }
   128	
   129	                break;
   130	
   131	            case Alignment.End:
   132	                switch (mode)
   133	                {
   134	                    case AlignmentModes.StartToEnd:
   135	                        return End (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive);
   136	
   137	                    case AlignmentModes.StartToEnd | AlignmentModes.IgnoreFirstOrLast:
   138	                        return IgnoreFirst (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive);
   139	
   140	                    case AlignmentModes.EndToStart:
   141	                        return Start (in sizesCopy, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive).Reverse ().ToArray ();
   142	
   143	                    case AlignmentModes.EndToStart | AlignmentModes.IgnoreFirstOrLast:
   144	                        return IgnoreLast (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive).Reverse ().ToArray ();
   145	                }
   146	
   147	                break;
   148	
   149	            case Alignment.Center:
   150	                mode &= ~AlignmentModes.IgnoreFirstOrLast;
   151	
   152	                switch (mode)
   153	                {
   154	                    case AlignmentModes.StartToEnd:
   155	                        return Center (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive);
   156	
   157	                    case AlignmentModes.EndToStart:
   158	                        return Center (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize, maxSpaceBetweenItems, spacesToGive).Reverse ().ToArray ();
   159	                }
   160	
   161	                break;
   162	
   163	            case Alignment.Fill:
   164	                mode &= ~AlignmentModes.IgnoreFirstOrLast;
   165	
   166	                switch (mode)
   167	                {
   168	                    case AlignmentModes.StartToEnd:
   169	                        return Fill (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize);
   170	
   171	                    case AlignmentModes.EndToStart:
   172	                        return Fill (in sizesCopy, containerSize, totalItemsSize).Reverse ().ToArray ();
   173	                }
   174	
   175	                break;
   176	
   177	            default:
   178	                throw new ArgumentOutOfRangeException (nameof (alignment), alignment, null);
   179	        }
   180	
   181	        return [];
   182	    }
   183	
   184	    internal static int [] Start (ref readonly int [] sizes, int maxSpaceBetweenItems, int spacesToGive)
   185	    {
   186	        var positions = new int [sizes.Length]; // positions of the items. the return value.
   187	
   188	        for (var i = 0; i < sizes.Length; i++)
   189	        {
   190	            CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (i, in sizes);
   191	
   192	            if (i == 0)
   193	            {
   194	                positions [0] = 0; // first item position
   195	
   196	                continue;
   197	            }
   198	
   199	            int spaceBefore = spacesToGive-- > 0 ? maxSpaceBetweenItems : 0;
   200	
   201	            // subsequent items are placed one space after the previous item
   202	            positions [i] = positions [i - 1] + sizes [i - 1] + spaceBefore;
   203	        }
   204	
   205	        return positions;
   206	    }
   207	
   208	    internal static int [] IgnoreFirst (ref readonly int [] sizes, int containerSize, int totalItemsSize, int maxSpaceBetweenItems, int spacesToGive)
   209	    {
   210	        var positions = new int [sizes.Length]; // positions of the items. the return value.
   211	
   212	        switch (sizes.Length)
   213	        {
   214	            case > 1:
   215	            {
   216	                var currentPosition = 0;
   217	                positions [0] = currentPosition; // first item is flush left
   218	
   219	                for (int i = sizes.Length - 1; i >= 0; i--)
   220	                {
   221	                    CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (i, in sizes);
   222	
   223	                    if (i == sizes.Length - 1)
   224	                    {
   225	                        // start at right
   226	                        currentPosition = Math.Max (totalItemsSize, containerSize) - sizes [i];
   227	                        positions [i] = currentPosition;
   228	                    }
   229	
   230	                    if (i >= sizes.Length - 1 || i <= 0)
   231	                    {
   232	                        continue;
   233	                    }
   234	                    int spaceBefore = spacesToGive-- > 0 ? maxSpaceBetweenItems : 0;
   235	
   236	                    positions [i] = currentPosition - sizes [i] - spaceBefore;
   237	                    currentPosition = positions [i];
   238	                }
   239	
   240	                break;
   241	            }
   242	
   243	            case 1:
   244	                CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (0, in sizes);
   245	                positions [0] = 0; // single item is flush left
   246	
   247	                break;
   248	        }
   249	
   250	        return positions;
   251	    }
   252	
   253	    internal static int [] IgnoreLast (ref readonly int [] sizes, int containerSize, int totalItemsSize, int maxSpaceBetweenItems, int spacesToGive)
   254	    {
   255	        var positions = new int [sizes.Length]; // positions of the items. the return value.
   256	
   257	        if (sizes.Length > 1)
   258	        {
   259	            var currentPosition = 0;
   260	
   261	            if (totalItemsSize > containerSize)
   262	            {
   263	                // Don't allow negative positions
   264	                currentPosition = int.Max (0, containerSize - totalItemsSize - spacesToGive);
   265	            }
   266	
   267	            for (var i = 0; i < sizes.Length; i++)
   268	            {
   269	                CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (i, in sizes);
   270	
   271	                if (i >= sizes.Length - 1)
   272	                {
   273	                    continue;
   274	                }
   275	                int spaceBefore = spacesToGive-- > 0 ? maxSpaceBetweenItems : 0;
   276	
   277	                positions [i] = currentPosition;
   278	                currentPosition += sizes [i] + spaceBefore;
   279	            }
   280	
   281	            positions [sizes.Length - 1] = containerSize - sizes [^1];
   282	        }
   283	        else if (sizes.Length == 1)
   284	        {
   285	            CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (0, in sizes);
   286	
   287	            positions [0] = containerSize - sizes [0]; // single item is flush right
   288	        }
   289	
   290	        return positions;
   291	    }
   292	
   293	    internal static int [] Fill (ref readonly int [] sizes, int containerSize, int totalItemsSize)
   294	    {
   295	        var positions = new int [sizes.Length]; // positions of the items. the return value.
   296	
   297	        int spaceBetween = sizes.Length > 1 ? (containerSize - totalItemsSize) / (sizes.Length - 1) : 0;
   298	        int remainder = sizes.Length > 1 ? (containerSize - totalItemsSize) % (sizes.Length - 1) : 0;
   299	        var currentPosition = 0;
   300	
   301	        for (var i = 0; i < sizes.Length; i++)
   302	        {
   303	            CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (i, in sizes);
   304	            positions [i] = currentPosition;
   305	            int extraSpace = i < remainder ? 1 : 0;
   306	            currentPosition += sizes [i] + spaceBetween + extraSpace;
   307	        }
   308	
   309	        return positions;
   310	    }
   311	
   312	    internal static int [] Center (ref readonly int [] sizes, int containerSize, int totalItemsSize, int maxSpaceBetweenItems, int spacesToGive)
   313	    {
   314	        var positions = new int [sizes.Length]; // positions of the items. the return value.
   315	
   316	        if (sizes.Length > 1)
   317	        {
   318	            // remaining space to be distributed before first and after the items
   319	            int remainingSpace = containerSize - totalItemsSize - spacesToGive;
   320	
   321	            for (var i = 0; i < sizes.Length; i++)
   322	            {
   323	                CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (i, in sizes);
   324	
   325	                if (i == 0)
   326	                {
   327	                    positions [i] = remainingSpace / 2; // first item position
   328	
   329	                    continue;
   330	                }
   331	
   332	                int spaceBefore = spacesToGive-- > 0 ? maxSpaceBetweenItems : 0;
   333	
   334	                // subsequent items are placed one space after the previous item
   335	                positions [i] = positions [i - 1] + sizes [i - 1] + spaceBefore;
   336	            }
   337	        }
   338	        else if (sizes.Length == 1)
   339	        {
   340	            CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (0, in sizes);
   341	            positions [0] = (containerSize - sizes [0]) / 2; // single item is centered
   342	        }
   343	
   344	        return positions;
   345	    }
   346	
   347	    internal static int [] End (ref readonly int [] sizes, int containerSize, int totalItemsSize, int maxSpaceBetweenItems, int spacesToGive)
   348	    {
   349	        var positions = new int [sizes.Length]; // positions of the items. the return value.
   350	        int currentPosition = containerSize - totalItemsSize - spacesToGive;
   351	
   352	        for (var i = 0; i < sizes.Length; i++)
   353	        {
   354	            CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (i, in sizes);
   355	            int spaceBefore = spacesToGive-- > 0 ? maxSpaceBetweenItems : 0;
   356	
   357	            positions [i] = currentPosition;
   358	            currentPosition += sizes [i] + spaceBefore;
   359	        }
   360	
   361	        return positions;
   362	    }
   363	
   364	    private static void CheckSizeCannotBeNegative (int i, ref readonly int [] sizes)
   365	    {
   366	        if (sizes [i] < 0)
   367	        {
   368	            throw new ArgumentException ("The size of an item cannot be negative.");
   369	        }
   370	    }
   371	}

Now I have a clear picture. The issue is in `SetLayout()` vs the auto-size calculation.

For horizontal orientation, `SetLayout()` sets:
- `X = Pos.Align(Alignment.Start, AlignmentModes.StartToEnd)` 
- `Width = Dim.Auto()`

The `Pos.Align` with `Alignment.Start` and `AlignmentModes.StartToEnd` distributes items from left to right. The `Aligner.Start` method places first item at position 0, second at position 0 + size of first, etc.

The problem is: the parent's `DimAuto(Content)` calculation needs to know the total width of all children. But with `PosAlign`, the children's X positions depend on the container size (the parent's width), which is what we're trying to calculate! This is a circular dependency.

Actually wait - let me look at `CalculateMinDimension` again:

```csharp
public static int CalculateMinDimension (int groupId, IReadOnlyCollection<View> views, Dimension dimension)
{
    var dimensionsSum = 0;
    foreach (View view in views)
    {
        if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            continue;
        PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;
        if (posAlign is { })
        {
            dimensionsSum += dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.Frame.Width : view.Frame.Height;
        }
    }
    return dimensionsSum;
}
```

This sums `Frame.Width` of all views in the alignment group. But `Frame.Width` is the already-calculated frame width. If the views haven't been laid out yet, this is 0.

BUT - the views are also in `DimAutoBased` category, and `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` is called with them:

```csharp
maxCalculatedSize = CalculateMaxSizeFromList (categories.DimAutoBased, maxCalculatedSize, dimension);
```

Which does:
```csharp
int newMax = dimension == Dimension.Width
                 ? v.Frame.X + v.Width.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension)
                 : ...
```

Here, `v.Width.Calculate(0, max, v, dimension)` will compute the auto width of the checkbox (e.g., text width). `v.Frame.X` is still 0 (not calculated yet). So `newMax` = 0 + checkboxWidth.

Then `maxCalculatedSize` becomes the max of the individual checkbox widths. But the total width needed is the SUM of all checkbox widths (plus spacing), not the MAX.

BUT `CalculateMinDimension` is supposed to compute the sum! However, at the time it's called, `Frame.Width` is 0 for all views. So `dimensionsSum` = 0.

The order in `Calculate` is:
1. `NotDependent` - processes and calls `SetRelativeLayout`, computing frame sizes
2. ... `AlignGroupIds` - calls `CalculateMinDimension` which sums `Frame.Width` - but these views weren't in `NotDependent`, so their frames haven't been computed yet!

So the fix should be: either call `SetRelativeLayout` on the aligned views before computing `CalculateMinDimension`, OR change the order so that `DimAutoBased` views are processed before `AlignGroupIds`.

But wait, there's another issue. Even if we fix the order, `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` for `DimAutoBased` views only takes the max, not the sum. But the align calculation should give us the sum (since aligned views are laid out sequentially).

Let me look at this from a simpler angle. The real fix suggested by the PR description is: after `CreateSubViews()` rebuilds the child views, the parent's auto width needs to be recalculated. The most straightforward fix would be to call `SetNeedsLayout()` in `CreateSubViews()` after the layout is set up.

But actually, `SetNeedsLayout()` IS already called by the `Add` method. So maybe the issue is something else entirely.

Let me look at what happens when `Layout()` is called on the selector. The layout system should compute the auto width. Let me look at `View.Layout()`:

    ///         layout.
    ///     </para>
    /// </remarks>
    /// <value>
    ///     <see langword="true"/> if layout is needed.
    /// </value>
    public bool NeedsLayout { get; internal set; } = true;

    /// <summary>
    ///     Sets <see cref="NeedsLayout"/> to return <see langword="true"/>, indicating this View and all of it's subviews
    ///     (including adornments) need to be laid out in the next Application iteration.
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    ///     <para>
    ///         The next iteration will cause <see cref="Layout()"/> to be called on the next
    ///         <see cref="IApplication.Iteration"/> so there is normally no reason to call see <see cref="Layout()"/>.
    ///     </para>
    /// </remarks>
    public void SetNeedsLayout ()
    {
        NeedsLayout = true;

        if (Margin.View is { SubViews.Count: > 0 })
        {
            Margin.View.SetNeedsLayout ();
        }

        if (Border.View is { SubViews.Count: > 0 })
        {
            Border.View.SetNeedsLayout ();
        }

        if (Padding.View is { SubViews.Count: > 0 })
        {
            Padding.View.SetNeedsLayout ();
        }

        // TODO: Optimize this - see Setting_Thickness_Causes_Adornment_SubView_Layout
        // Use a stack to avoid recursion
        Stack<View> stack = new (InternalSubViews.Snapshot ().ToList ());

        while (stack.Count > 0)
        {
            Debug.Assert (stack.Peek () is { });

            View current = stack.Pop ();

            if (current.NeedsLayout)
            {
                continue;
            }
            current.NeedsLayout = true;

            if (current.Margin.View is { SubViews.Count: > 0 })
            {
                current.Margin.View.SetNeedsLayout ();
            }

            if (current.Border.View is { SubViews.Count: > 0 })
            {
                current.Border.View.SetNeedsLayout ();
            }

            if (current.Padding.View is { SubViews.Count: > 0 })
            {
                current.Padding.View.SetNeedsLayout ();
            }

            foreach (View subview in current.SubViews)
            {
                stack.Push (subview);
            }
        }

        TextFormatter.NeedsFormat = true;

        if (SuperView is { NeedsLayout: false })
        {
            SuperView?.SetNeedsLayout ();
        }

        if (this is not AdornmentView adornment)
        {
            return;
        }

        if (adornment.Adornment?.Parent is { NeedsLayout: false })
        {
            adornment.Adornment.Parent?.SetNeedsLayout ();
        }
    }

    #endregion NeedsLayout

    /// <summary>
    ///     INTERNAL API - Sets _frame, calls SetsNeedsLayout, and raises OnViewportChanged/ViewportChanged
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="frame"></param>
    /// <returns><see langword="true"/> if the frame was changed.</returns>
    private bool SetFrame (in Rectangle frame)
    {
        if (_frame == frame)
        {
            return false;
        }

        var oldViewport = Rectangle.Empty;

        if (IsInitialized)
        {
            oldViewport = Viewport;
        }

        // This is the only place where _frame should be set directly. Use Frame = or SetFrame instead.
        _frame = frame;

        // Set the Margin's Frame. All other Adornments use this.
        Margin.View?.Frame = Frame with { Location = Point.Empty };

        SetNeedsDraw ();
        SetNeedsLayout ();

        // BUGBUG: When SetFrame is called from Frame_set, this event gets raised BEFORE OnResizeNeeded. Is that OK?
        OnFrameChanged (in frame);
        FrameChanged?.Invoke (this, new EventArgs<Rectangle> (in frame));

        if (oldViewport != Viewport)
        {
            RaiseViewportChangedEvent (oldViewport);
        }

        return true;
    }

    /// <summary>
    ///     Called when <see cref="Frame"/> changes.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="frame">The new Frame.</param>
    protected virtual void OnFrameChanged (in Rectangle frame) { }

    /// <summary>
    ///     Raised when the <see cref="Frame"/> changes. This event is raised after the <see cref="Frame"/> has been
    ///     updated.
    /// </summary>
    public event EventHandler<EventArgs<Rectangle>>? FrameChanged;

    /// <summary>Gets the <see cref="Frame"/> with a screen-relative location.</summary>
    /// <returns>The location and size of the view in screen-relative coordinates.</returns>
    public virtual Rectangle FrameToScreen ()
    {
        Rectangle screen = Frame;
        View? current = SuperView;

        while (current is { })
        {
            if (current is AdornmentView adornment)
            {
                // Adornments don't have SuperViews; use Adornment.FrameToScreen override
                // which will give us the screen coordinates of the parent

                Rectangle parentScreen = adornment.FrameToScreen ();

                // Now add our Frame location
                parentScreen.Offset (screen.X, screen.Y);

                return parentScreen with { Size = Frame.Size };
            }

            Point viewportOffset = current.GetViewportOffsetFromFrame ();
            viewportOffset.Offset (current.Frame.X - current.Viewport.X, current.Frame.Y - current.Viewport.Y);
            screen.X += viewportOffset.X;
            screen.Y += viewportOffset.Y;
            current = current.SuperView;
        }

        return screen;
    }

    /// <summary>
    ///     Converts a screen-relative coordinate to a Frame-relative coordinate. Frame-relative means relative to the
    ///     View's <see cref="SuperView"/>'s <see cref="Viewport"/>.
    /// </summary>
    /// <returns>The coordinate relative to the <see cref="SuperView"/>'s <see cref="Viewport"/>.</returns>
    /// <param name="location">Screen-relative coordinate.</param>
    public virtual Point ScreenToFrame (in Point location)
    {
        if (SuperView is null)
        {
            return new Point (location.X - Frame.X, location.Y - Frame.Y);
        }

        Point superViewViewportOffset = SuperView.GetViewportOffsetFromFrame ();
        superViewViewportOffset.Offset (-SuperView.Viewport.X, -SuperView.Viewport.Y);

        Point frame = location;
        frame.Offset (-superViewViewportOffset.X, -superViewViewportOffset.Y);

        frame = SuperView.ScreenToFrame (frame);
        frame.Offset (-Frame.X, -Frame.Y);

        return frame;
    }

    public Dim Width
    {
        get => _width;
        set
        {
            CWPPropertyHelper.ChangeProperty (this,
                                              ref _width,
                                              value,
                                              OnWidthChanging,
                                              WidthChanging,
                                              newValue =>
                                              {
                                                  _width = newValue;

                                                  // Reset TextFormatter - Will be recalculated in SetTextFormatterSize
                                                  TextFormatter.ConstrainToWidth = null;
                                                  PosDimSet ();
                                              },
                                              OnWidthChanged,
                                              WidthChanged,
                                              out Dim _);

            NeedsClearScreenNextIteration ();
        }
    }

    private void NeedsClearScreenNextIteration ()
    {
        if (App?.SessionStack?.Select (r => r.Runnable as View).Count () == 1)
        {
            // this is the root IRunnable; we need to redraw the screen
            App?.ClearScreenNextIteration = true;
        }
    }

    /// <summary>
    ///     Called before the <see cref="Width"/> property changes, allowing subclasses to cancel or modify the change.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="args">The event arguments containing the current and proposed new width.</param>
    /// <returns>True to cancel the change, false to proceed.</returns>
    protected virtual bool OnWidthChanging (ValueChangingEventArgs<Dim> args) => false;

    /// <summary>
    ///     Called after the <see cref="Width"/> property changes, allowing subclasses to react to the change.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="args">The event arguments containing the old and new width.</param>
    protected virtual void OnWidthChanged (ValueChangedEventArgs<Dim> args) { }

    /// <summary>

2026-05-29 16:42:19,662 - DEBUG - swea-lm-gui-cs__Terminal.Gui-4860 - total_tokens_sent=1,098,600, total_tokens_received=6,715, total_cost=0.00, total_api_calls=39
2026-05-29 16:42:19,664 - INFO - swea-agent-gui-cs__Terminal.Gui-4860 - 💭 THOUGHT
So setting `Width` calls `PosDimSet()` which calls `SetNeedsLayout()`:

```csharp
private void PosDimSet ()
{
    SetNeedsLayout ();
    ...
}
```

And `SetNeedsLayout()` calls `SuperView?.SetNeedsLayout()` if the parent doesn't already need layout. So changing a subview's Width DOES trigger the parent.

But wait - `SetLayout()` calls:
```csharp
SubViews.ElementAt(i).Width = Dim.Auto ();
```

This triggers `SetNeedsLayout()` on the subview, which triggers `SetNeedsLayout()` on the parent (the selector). So the parent should be marked as needing layout.

Hmm, let me think about this differently. Maybe the issue is NOT about `SetNeedsLayout` not being called, but about the layout calculation itself producing wrong results.

Let me try to actually run the existing tests to understand the framework

#!/usr/bin/env dotnet-script

using Terminal.Gui;

using Terminal.Gui.ViewBase;

var selector = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Horizontal,
};

selector.Labels = ["IMDb (Recommended)", "TMDb"];
selector.Values = [0, 1];

Console.WriteLine($"Before Layout - Selector Frame: {selector.Frame}");

selector.Layout();

Console.WriteLine($"After Layout - Selector Frame: {selector.Frame}");

Console.WriteLine("\nSubViews:");
foreach (var cb in selector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  {cb.Title}: Frame={cb.Frame}, Width={cb.Width}");
}

// Expected: Frame.Width should be >= sum of both checkbox widths
EOF

using Terminal.Gui;
using Terminal.Gui.Views;
using Terminal.Gui.ViewBase;

var selector = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Horizontal,
};

selector.Labels = ["IMDb (Recommended)", "TMDb"];
selector.Values = [0, 1];

Console.WriteLine($"Before Layout - Selector Frame: {selector.Frame}");
Console.WriteLine($"Before Layout - Selector NeedsLayout: {selector.NeedsLayout}");

selector.Layout();

Console.WriteLine($"After Layout - Selector Frame: {selector.Frame}");

Console.WriteLine("\nSubViews:");
foreach (var cb in selector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  {cb.Title}: Frame={cb.Frame}, Width={cb.Width}");
}

// Now let's also test the scenario from PR description - adding to a parent
var win = new Window { Title = "Repro" };
win.Add(selector);
win.Layout();

Console.WriteLine($"\nAfter adding to window and layout:");
Console.WriteLine($"  Selector Frame: {selector.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  {cb.Title}: Frame={cb.Frame}");
}
EOF

Interesting! The first `Layout()` gives `Width=22` which is only the width of the first checkbox. After adding to window and laying out again, it gives `Width=28` which is sum of both (22 + 6). The second layout also shows correct X positions.

So the issue is that the first `selector.Layout()` doesn't compute the correct width. Let me investigate why. The first layout gives:
- First checkbox: X=0, Width=22
- Second checkbox: X=22, Width=6
- Selector Width=22 (not 28!)

The selector width should be 22 + 6 = 28 (or maybe plus the horizontal space of 2 between them = 30). But it's 22.

Wait, looking at the output, the second checkbox is at X=22 and has Width=6. The selector's width should be at least 22 + 6 = 28. But it's 22. The first layout gives wrong results.

After adding to window and doing `win.Layout()`, the selector width becomes 28. So the second layout works correctly.

This confirms the bug! The first `Layout()` call after setting Labels/Values gives wrong width. The second layout (after adding to a parent) works.

Now why does the first layout fail? Let me think...

The `Layout()` method computes the frame. For the selector with `Width = Dim.Auto(DimAutoStyle.Content)`:

1. `Calculate` is called with `superviewContentSize` (probably 0 or some default)
2. It iterates subviews and computes sizes

At the first layout, the `superviewContentSize` might be 0. Let me check what `superviewContentSize` is used. In `DimAuto.Calculate`:

```csharp
int autoMin = MinimumContentDim?.GetAnchor (superviewContentSize) ?? 0;
int screenX4 = dimension == Dimension.Width ? screenSize.Width * 4 : screenSize.Height * 4;
int autoMax = MaximumContentDim?.GetAnchor (superviewContentSize) ?? screenX4;
```

Since there's no `MaximumContentDim` or `MinimumContentDim`, `autoMax = screenX4 = 2048 * 4 = 8192`.

Then for `Content` style, it processes views. The `superviewContentSize` is passed through to each view's `Calculate`. For the checkbox width calculation, it's `v.Width.Calculate(0, max, v, dimension)` where `max` starts at 0 and grows.

But the key issue might be in how `PosAlign` interacts with this. Let me check: in `CalculateMaxSizeFromList`:

```csharp
int newMax = dimension == Dimension.Width
                 ? v.Frame.X + v.Width.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension)
                 : ...
```

`v.Frame.X` is 0 before the PosAlign calculation. `v.Width.Calculate` returns the checkbox's text width (e.g., 22 for "IMDb (Recommended)"). So `newMax` = 0 + 22 = 22 for the first checkbox. For the second, `newMax` = 0 + 6 = 6. The max is 22.

Then `CalculateMinDimension` for aligned views: `dimensionsSum += view.Frame.Width`. But `Frame.Width` is still 0 because `SetRelativeLayout` hasn't been called on these views (they're not in `NotDependent`). So `maxAlign` = 0.

Final: `max = int.Max(textSize, maxCalculatedSize)` = max(0, 22) = 22.

So the first layout produces width=22.

Now after adding to window and laying out again, why does it work? Because on the second layout:
- `PosAlign._cachedLocation` might still have the old cached values
- Or the views have been properly laid out from the first pass, so `Frame.Width` now has correct values

Wait, after the first layout, the frames are set. Let me check: after first `Layout()`:
- Checkbox 1: Frame={X=0,Y=0,Width=22,Height=1} 
- Checkbox 2: Frame={X=22,Y=0,Width=6,Height=1}

The X positions are correct! The PosAlign DID compute correctly. But the selector's width is wrong (22 instead of 28).

So PosAlign works fine - it places items correctly at X=0 and X=22. But the parent's auto-width doesn't account for the sum. The `CalculateMinDimension` returns 0 because `Frame.Width` is 0 at the time it's called.

On the second layout:
- `Frame.Width` is now 22 and 6 (from the first layout)
- `CalculateMinDimension` returns 22 + 6 = 28
- `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` returns max(0+22, 0+6) = 22 (or maybe 22+6=28 from the X positions)

Actually, wait. Let me re-read `CalculateMaxSizeFromList`:

```csharp
int newMax = dimension == Dimension.Width
                 ? v.Frame.X + v.Width.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension)
                 : ...
```

On the second layout, `v.Frame.X` is 22 for the second checkbox (from the first layout). So `newMax` = 22 + 6 = 28. That gives 28. And `CalculateMinDimension` would also give 22 + 6 = 28. So both paths give 28.

So the fix should ensure that `CalculateMinDimension` works correctly even on the first layout. The issue is that `CalculateMinDimension` uses `Frame.Width` which hasn't been computed yet.

But actually, looking at the order in `DimAuto.Calculate`:
1. `NotDependent` views are processed first (with `SetRelativeLayout`)
2. Then `AlignGroupIds` is processed

The problem is that checkboxes with `PosAlign` X and `DimAuto` Width are NOT in `NotDependent` (because `PosAlign.DependsOnSuperViewContentSize` is true). So they don't get `SetRelativeLayout` called before `CalculateMinDimension`.

The fix could be:
1. In `DimAuto.Calculate`, process `DimAutoBased` views before `AlignGroupIds`, so that `SetRelativeLayout` gets called and frames are computed. But wait, `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` doesn't call `SetRelativeLayout` either.

Actually, let me check what `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` does:

```csharp
private static int CalculateMaxSizeFromList (List<View> views, int max, Dimension dimension)
{
    foreach (View v in views)
    {
        int newMax = dimension == Dimension.Width
                         ? v.Frame.X + v.Width.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension)
                         : v.Frame.Y + v.Height.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension);
        if (newMax > max)
        {
            max = newMax;
        }
    }
    return max;
}
```

It doesn't call `SetRelativeLayout` either! It just uses `v.Frame.X` and `v.Width.Calculate`. The `Width.Calculate` for `DimAuto` will compute the text width correctly. But `Frame.X` may not be set yet.

So after `CalculateMaxSizeFromList`, the frames are NOT updated. Only `NotDependent` views have `SetRelativeLayout` called.

Then when `CalculateMinDimension` is called, `Frame.Width` is still 0 for all views.

The fix should be to call `SetRelativeLayout` for the aligned views before computing `CalculateMinDimension`, OR to compute the sum differently (like calling `Width.Calculate` for each view instead of using `Frame.Width`).

Actually, looking at `CalculateMinDimension`:

```csharp
public static int CalculateMinDimension (int groupId, IReadOnlyCollection<View> views, Dimension dimension)
{
    var dimensionsSum = 0;
    foreach (View view in views)
    {
        if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            continue;
        PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;
        if (posAlign is { })
        {
            dimensionsSum += dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.Frame.Width : view.Frame.Height;
        }
    }
    return dimensionsSum;
}
```

This should use `view.Width.Calculate(...)` instead of `view.Frame.Width`, because `Frame.Width` may not be computed yet. But `Width.Calculate` needs appropriate parameters.

Actually, wait. This is a deeper issue in the `DimAuto.Calculate` logic. But maybe there's a simpler fix for the SelectorBase. 

Let me re-think the PR description. It says:

> Root cause (suspected): `SelectorBase` sets `Width = Dim.Auto(DimAutoStyle.Content)` in the constructor (line 38). The `Labels` setter calls `CreateSubViews()` which rebuilds child checkboxes, but the parent's auto width doesn't pick up the new content size until a focus-driven layout pass.

So the fix could be to call `SetNeedsLayout()` explicitly in `CreateSubViews()`. But as I showed, `SetNeedsLayout()` IS called by the `Add` method. The issue is that even with `SetNeedsLayout()` called, when `Layout()` runs, it computes the wrong size on the first pass.

But wait - after adding to window, the second layout works. Let me check if maybe the issue is that `Layout()` needs to be called twice, or if there's a caching issue.

So the first layout partially works - it positions the children correctly but doesn't compute the parent's width correctly.

The second layout fixes the parent width. So maybe the solution is to call `Layout()` twice? No, that's hacky.

Let me look at this from the `DimAuto.Calculate` perspective. The issue is that when computing auto-width for the parent:

1. `NotDependent` views are laid out first (calling `SetRelativeLayout`). But checkboxes with PosAlign are NOT in this category.
2. `AlignGroupIds` calls `CalculateMinDimension` which uses `Frame.Width` - still 0.
3. `DimAutoBased` calls `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` which uses `Frame.X + Width.Calculate(...)`. Frame.X is 0, so this gives max of individual widths.

The fix in `DimAuto.Calculate` would be to ensure views have their frames computed before `CalculateMinDimension`. But modifying the core layout system might have unintended side effects. Let me see if there's a simpler fix specific to `SelectorBase`.

Actually, looking at the `SetLayout()` method in `SelectorBase`:

```csharp
protected void SetLayout ()
{
    ...
    for (var i = 0; i < SubViews.Count; i++)
    {
        if (Orientation == Orientation.Vertical)
        {
            ...
            SubViews.ElementAt(i).Width = Dim.Func (_ => maxNaturalCheckBoxWidth);
        }
        else
        {
            SubViews.ElementAt(i).X = Pos.Align (Alignment.Start, AlignmentModes.StartToEnd);
            SubViews.ElementAt(i).Y = 0;
            SubViews.ElementAt(i).Margin.Thickness = new Thickness (0, 0, i < SubViews.Count - 1 ? _horizontalSpace : 0, 0);
            SubViews.ElementAt(i).Width = Dim.Auto ();
        }
    }
}
```

For horizontal orientation, it sets `X = Pos.Align(...)`. This makes the subviews dependent on the parent's content size, creating a circular dependency: parent width depends on children positions, but children positions depend on parent width.

What if we changed the horizontal layout to NOT use `Pos.Align` and instead use a different approach? Like using `Pos.Absolute` with computed positions? But then we'd need to know the widths upfront.

Alternatively, what if we just call `SetNeedsLayout()` at the end of `CreateSubViews()`? It's already called by `Add`, but maybe the issue is that the `SetLayout()` changes happen after the `Add` calls, and the `SetLayout()` changes (setting Width, X) trigger `SetNeedsLayout()` on the parent, but the parent's `Layout()` might have already run or the layout system might coalesce multiple `SetNeedsLayout()` calls.

Actually, I think the real fix should be in `CreateSubViews()` - after all the setup is done, we should ensure the parent's layout is invalidated. But since `Add` already calls `SetNeedsLayout()`, maybe the issue is that `SetNeedsLayout()` is called but `Layout()` doesn't run until later, and when it does run, it produces wrong results due to the `DimAuto.Calculate` issue I identified.

Let me try a different approach: instead of fixing the core layout system, let me see if there's a way to fix the `SelectorBase` to avoid the problem. For instance, for horizontal orientation, instead of using `Pos.Align`, we could set `X` positions explicitly after computing widths.

But that might be a bigger change. Let me look at what the PR description suggests as a workaround: "Setting `Width = Dim.Fill()` on the selector avoids the issue."

Maybe the fix is simply to have `CreateSubViews` call `SetNeedsLayout()` at the end, and also ensure that the layout runs properly. But wait, `SetNeedsLayout` is already called. Let me investigate whether the first `Layout()` call actually runs the full layout or if it short-circuits.

Actually, let me look at the `Layout()` method to see what happens:

    /// <summary>
    ///     Performs layout of the view and its subviews within the specified content size.
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    ///     <para>
    ///         See the View Layout Deep Dive for more information:
    ///         <see href="https://gui-cs.github.io/Terminal.Gui/docs/layout.html"/>
    ///     </para>
    ///     <para>
    ///         This method is intended to be called by the layout engine to
    ///         prepare the view for layout and is exposed as a public API primarily for testing purposes.
    ///     </para>
    /// </remarks>
    /// <param name="contentSize"></param>
    /// <returns><see langword="false"/>If the view could not be laid out (typically because a dependencies was not ready). </returns>
    public bool Layout (Size contentSize)
    {
        if (!SetRelativeLayout (contentSize))
        {
            return false;
        }
        LayoutSubViews ();

        // A layout was performed so a draw is needed
        // NeedsLayout may still be true if a dependent View still needs layout after SubViewsLaidOut event
        SetNeedsDraw ();

        return true;
    }

                newW = _width.Calculate (newX, superviewContentSize.Width, this, Dimension.Width);
            }

            if (_height.Has<DimAuto> (out _))
            {
                newH = _height.Calculate (0, superviewContentSize.Height, this, Dimension.Height);
                newY = _y.Calculate (superviewContentSize.Height, newH, this, Dimension.Height);

                if (newH != Frame.Height)
                {
                    // Pos.Calculate got us a new position. We need to redo dimension
                    newH = _height.Calculate (newY, superviewContentSize.Height, this, Dimension.Height);
                }
            }
            else
            {
                newY = _y.Calculate (superviewContentSize.Height, _height, this, Dimension.Height);
                newH = _height.Calculate (newY, superviewContentSize.Height, this, Dimension.Height);
            }
        }
        catch (LayoutException)
        {
            //Debug.WriteLine ($"A Dim/PosFunc function threw (typically this is because a dependent View was not laid out)\n{le}.");
            return false;
        }

        Rectangle newFrame = new (newX, newY, newW, newH);

            if (_x is PosAbsolute)

    private void CheckDimAuto ()
    {
        if (!ValidatePosDim || !IsInitialized)
        {
            return;
        }

        var widthAuto = Width as DimAuto;
        var heightAuto = Height as DimAuto;

        // Verify none of the subviews are using Dim objects that depend on the SuperView's dimensions.
        foreach (View view in SubViews)
        {
            if (widthAuto is { } && widthAuto.Style.FastHasFlags (DimAutoStyle.Content) && ContentSizeTracksViewport)
            {
                ThrowInvalid (view, view.Width, nameof (view.Width));
                ThrowInvalid (view, view.X, nameof (view.X));
            }

            if (heightAuto is null || !heightAuto.Style.FastHasFlags (DimAutoStyle.Content) || !ContentSizeTracksViewport)
            {
                continue;
            }
            ThrowInvalid (view, view.Height, nameof (view.Height));
            ThrowInvalid (view, view.Y, nameof (view.Y));
        }

        return;

```csharp
public static int CalculateMinDimension (int groupId, IReadOnlyCollection<View> views, Dimension dimension)
{
    var dimensionsSum = 0;
    foreach (View view in views)
    {
        if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            continue;
        PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;
        if (posAlign is { })
        {
            dimensionsSum += dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.Frame.Width : view.Frame.Height;
        }
    }
    return dimensionsSum;
}
```

If I change `view.Frame.Width` to `view.Width.Calculate(0, 0, view, dimension)`, it would compute the width directly without needing a prior layout. But `Width.Calculate` needs `superviewContentSize` as its second parameter (after `location`). Let me check the signature:

```csharp
internal abstract int Calculate (int location, int superviewContentSize, View us, Dimension dimension);
```

So I'd need a valid `superviewContentSize`. For the purpose of computing minimum dimension, we could use something like `int.MaxValue` or the screen size. But that might not be correct for all cases.

Actually, looking at how `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` does it:
```csharp
int newMax = dimension == Dimension.Width
                 ? v.Frame.X + v.Width.Calculate (0, max, v, dimension)
                 : ...
```

It passes `max` (the current accumulated max) as `superviewContentSize`. For `DimAuto`, this parameter is used as the max bound. So passing a large value should be fine.

- positions[0] = 0
- positions[1] = 0 + 22 + 0 = 22

So the second checkbox is at X=22, which is within the parent width of 22? No, X=22 + Width=6 = 28, which extends beyond the parent width of 22.

- Parent width = 22
- Child 1: X=0, Width=22
- Child 2: X=22, Width=6 (extends beyond parent!)

- `CalculateMinDimension` returns 22 + 6 = 28
- `CalculateMaxSizeFromList`: for child 2, `Frame.X` = 22, `Width.Calculate` = 6, so newMax = 28
- Parent width = 28

```csharp
private void LayoutSubViews ()
{
    foreach (View v in SubViews)
    {
        if (!v.NeedsLayout)

            continue;
        }
        v.Layout (GetContentSize ());
```

```csharp
public bool Layout ()
{
    return Layout (GetContainerSize ());
}

public bool Layout (Size contentSize)
{
    if (!SetRelativeLayout (contentSize))
    {
        return false;
    }
    LayoutSubViews ();
    SetNeedsDraw ();
    return true;
}
```

`Layout()` doesn't check `NeedsLayout` - it always runs! Only `LayoutSubViews` checks `NeedsLayout` on subviews. So calling `Layout()` twice will run the layout computation twice.

So `Add` calls `SetNeedsLayout()` on the parent (win), not on the added child (selector). And `SetNeedsLayout` on the parent also calls `SetNeedsLayout` on subviews:

```csharp
public void SetNeedsLayout ()
{
    NeedsLayout = true;
    // ...
    foreach (View subview in SubViews)
    {
        stack.Push (subview);
    }
    // Then for each, sets NeedsLayout = true
}
```

Ah, I see! `SetNeedsLayout` propagates to all subviews! So when we call `win.Add(selector)`, it calls `SetNeedsLayout()` on win, which sets `NeedsLayout = true` on all subviews (including the selector). So the selector's `NeedsLayout` becomes true again. Then `win.Layout()` -> `LayoutSubViews()` will layout the selector again.

So the second layout fixes things. The first layout (explicit `selector.Layout()`) gave wrong results.

        foreach (View view in views)
        {
            if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            {
                continue;
            }

            PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;

            if (posAlign is { })

            }
        }

        // Align
        return dimensionsSum;
    }

Now I need to change this to compute widths directly. The `Dim.Calculate` method takes `(int location, int superviewContentSize, View us, Dimension dimension)`. For calculating the minimum dimension, we can use a large value for `superviewContentSize` (like the screen size).

But wait, I need to be careful. This is a core layout method and changing it could have ripple effects. Let me think about what the safest fix is.

Actually, looking at this problem again, there's another approach: in `SelectorBase.CreateSubViews`, after building subviews and calling `SetLayout()`, we could force a layout by calling `Layout()` twice. The first call sets up the subview frames, and the second call recomputes the parent size correctly.

But that's hacky. Let me look at the actual root cause more carefully.

The problem is in `DimAuto.Calculate` line 259:
```csharp
maxAlign = PosAlign.CalculateMinDimension (groupId, us.InternalSubViews.ToArray (), dimension);
```

This is called BEFORE the `DimAutoBased` views are processed (line 284):
```csharp
maxCalculatedSize = CalculateMaxSizeFromList (categories.DimAutoBased, maxCalculatedSize, dimension);
```

If I reorder these so that `DimAutoBased` is processed BEFORE `AlignGroupIds`, then the frames would be updated (via `Width.Calculate` inside `CalculateMaxSizeFromList`), and then `CalculateMinDimension` would have correct `Frame.Width` values.

But wait, `CalculateMaxSizeFromList` doesn't call `SetRelativeLayout` either. It just calls `Width.Calculate` which computes the value but doesn't update `Frame.Width`. So reordering wouldn't help.

Actually, the issue is that `Width.Calculate` for a `DimAuto` returns the correct width, but `Frame.Width` is not updated. The `CalculateMinDimension` uses `Frame.Width` which is stale.

Let me trace `Width.Calculate` for `DimAuto`:
```csharp
internal override int Calculate (int location, int superviewContentSize, View us, Dimension dimension)
{
    // ...
    if (Style.FastHasFlags (DimAutoStyle.Text))
    {
        // computes textSize
    }
    if (Style.FastHasFlags (DimAutoStyle.Content))
    {
        // for subviews, etc.
    }
    // ...
}
```

For a `CheckBox`, `Width = Dim.Auto(DimAutoStyle.Text)` (set in CheckBox constructor). So it only has `DimAutoStyle.Text`, not `Content`. The text calculation:
- For width: `us.TextFormatter.FormatAndGetSize(new Size(int.Min(autoMax, screenX4), screenX4)).Width`

This returns the correct text width. But it doesn't set `Frame.Width`.

So the fix for `CalculateMinDimension` should be to use `Width.Calculate` instead of `Frame.Width`:

```csharp
public static int CalculateMinDimension (int groupId, IReadOnlyCollection<View> views, Dimension dimension)
{
    var dimensionsSum = 0;
    foreach (View view in views)
    {
        if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            continue;
        PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;
        if (posAlign is { })
        {
            // Calculate the dimension directly instead of relying on Frame, which may not be computed yet
            int size = dimension == Dimension.Width 
                ? view.Width.Calculate (0, 0, view, dimension) 
                : view.Height.Calculate (0, 0, view, dimension);
            dimensionsSum += size;
        }
    }
    return dimensionsSum;
}
```

But I need to verify that `Width.Calculate(0, 0, view, dimension)` works correctly. The second parameter is `superviewContentSize`. For `DimAuto`, this is used as:
- `autoMax = MaximumContentDim?.GetAnchor(superviewContentSize) ?? screenX4`

If `superviewContentSize` is 0, `autoMax` becomes `screenX4` (which is 2048*4 = 8192), which should be fine for computing text width.

But wait, there's another issue. `Calculate` for `DimAuto` also calls `TextFormatter.FormatAndGetSize` which has side effects (sets `ConstrainToSize`). Multiple calls might have issues. But this is probably fine.

Let me check if there are any tests that would break with this change:
