Let me check `SetNeedsLayout` and how it affects `ConstrainToWidth`:

Looking at `SetNeedsLayout` (line 848):
```csharp
TextFormatter.NeedsFormat = true;
```

And when `Width` is set:
```csharp
TextFormatter.ConstrainToWidth = null;
```

So after `SetNeedsLayout` is called, `NeedsFormat = true` but `ConstrainToWidth` remains whatever it was (may be null or may have a value). When `DimAuto.Calculate` is called:
- It checks `ConstrainToWidth is null` - if null, it computes and sets it
- If not null, it uses the cached value

After the first `Calculate` call, `ConstrainToWidth` is set. The second call uses the cached value. So there shouldn't be side effects from calling `Calculate` multiple times.

But wait, after `SetNeedsLayout` (which sets `NeedsFormat = true`), would `FormatAndGetSize` produce different results? Let me check `FormatAndGetSize`:

```csharp
public Size FormatAndGetSize (Size constrainTo)
{
    if (string.IsNullOrEmpty (Text) || ConstrainToWidth is 0 || ConstrainToHeight is 0)
    {
        NeedsFormat = false;
        return Size.Empty;
    }

    if (!NeedsFormat)
    {
        return new Size (ConstrainToWidth ?? int.MaxValue, ConstrainToHeight ?? int.MaxValue);
    }

    int width = ConstrainToWidth ?? int.MaxValue;
    // ...
}
```

So if `NeedsFormat` is false, it returns the cached sizes. But `SetNeedsLayout` sets `NeedsFormat = true`. However, `DimAuto.Calculate` first checks `ConstrainToWidth is null`:
```csharp
if (us.TextFormatter.ConstrainToWidth is null)
{
    us.TextFormatter.ConstrainToSize = us.TextFormatter.FormatAndGetSize (...);
}
```

So if `ConstrainToWidth` is not null (cached from a previous calculation), it uses the cached value. Even if `NeedsFormat` is true, `FormatAndGetSize` returns early if `ConstrainToWidth` is not null (since the condition checks `ConstrainToWidth is null` first... wait no, it doesn't. Let me re-read).

Actually, the outer condition in `DimAuto.Calculate` checks `ConstrainToWidth is null`:
```csharp
if (us.TextFormatter.ConstrainToWidth is null)
{
    us.TextFormatter.ConstrainToSize = us.TextFormatter.FormatAndGetSize (new Size (int.Min (autoMax, screenX4), screenX4));
}
textSize = us.TextFormatter.ConstrainToWidth ?? 0;
```

So if `ConstrainToWidth` was already computed, it's reused. If it's null, it's computed. After `SetNeedsLayout`, `ConstrainToWidth` is NOT reset (only `NeedsFormat` is set to true). So the second call to `Calculate` would still use the cached value.

But wait, `Width.set` does reset `ConstrainToWidth` to null. And `SetLayout()` calls `SubViews.ElementAt(i).Width = Dim.Auto()` which goes through the setter and resets `ConstrainToWidth`. So after `SetLayout()`, the subviews' `ConstrainToWidth` is null.

So the first `Layout()` call:
1. `DimAuto.Calculate` for parent width:
   - For each subview, `Width.Calculate` is called
   - Sets `ConstrainToWidth` for each subview (first time)
2. `CalculateMinDimension` uses `Frame.Width` which is 0 (bad)
3. Parent width computed incorrectly

Second `Layout()` call (after `SetNeedsLayout` from `win.Add`):
1. `DimAuto.Calculate` for parent width:
   - For each subview, `Width.Calculate` is called again
   - `ConstrainToWidth` is already set (from first pass), so uses cached value
   - `CalculateMinDimension` now sees `Frame.Width` = 22 and 6 (from first pass subview layout)
   - Parent width = 28 (correct)

So the issue is that `CalculateMinDimension` uses `Frame.Width` which is stale on the first pass. My proposed fix (using `Width.Calculate` directly) should work.

        {
            if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            {
                continue;
            }

            PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;

            if (posAlign is { })
            {
                dimensionsSum += dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.Frame.Width : view.Frame.Height;
            }
        }

        // Align
        return dimensionsSum;
    }'''

new = '''    // TODO: PosAlign.CalculateMinDimension is a hack. Need to figure out a better way of doing this.
    /// <summary>
    ///     Returns the minimum size a group of views with the same <paramref name="groupId"/> can be.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="groupId"></param>
    /// <param name="views"></param>
    /// <param name="dimension"></param>
    /// <returns></returns>
    public static int CalculateMinDimension (int groupId, IReadOnlyCollection<View> views, Dimension dimension)
    {
        var dimensionsSum = 0;

        foreach (View view in views)
        {
            if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            {
                continue;
            }

            PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;

            if (posAlign is { })
            {
                // Calculate the dimension directly instead of relying on Frame,
                // which may not have been computed yet (e.g., on first layout pass).
                dimensionsSum += dimension == Dimension.Width
                                     ? view.Width.Calculate (0, 0, view, dimension)
                                     : view.Height.Calculate (0, 0, view, dimension);
            }
        }

        // Align
        return dimensionsSum;
    }'''

if old in content:
    content = content.replace(old, new)
    with open('/testbed/Terminal.Gui/ViewBase/Layout/PosAlign.cs', 'w') as f:
        f.write(content)
    print("SUCCESS: File patched")
else:
    print("FAILED: Could not find old string in file")
    # Try to find it
    if 'CalculateMinDimension' in content:
        print("Found CalculateMinDimension in file")
    if '// TODO: PosAlign.CalculateMinDimension is a hack' in content:
        print("Found TODO comment")

2026-05-29 17:00:24,947 - INFO - swea-agent-gui-cs__Terminal.Gui-4860 - 💭 THOUGHT
Let me try to just run all tests and see if any fail. But that might take too long. Let me just run a few more key tests and then move on.

Given the limited test infrastructure available, and the fact that the change is minimal (just using `Width.Calculate` instead of `Frame.Width` in `CalculateMinDimension`), I'm fairly confident the fix is correct. The `Width.Calculate` method computes the same value that would eventually end up in `Frame.Width` after layout.

Now let me also think about edge cases:

1. **Vertical orientation**: The `SetLayout()` for vertical uses `Dim.Func(_ => maxNaturalCheckBoxWidth)` which doesn't use `PosAlign`. So `CalculateMinDimension` is not called for vertical orientation. No impact.

2. **When `Labels` is set before `Values`**: `CreateSubViews()` returns early because of count mismatch. No subviews created, no issue.

3. **When `Values` is set before `Labels`**: Same as above.

4. **When `Labels` is set to null**: `CreateSubViews()` returns early, no subviews. No issue.

5. **`SetValuesAndLabels<TEnum>()`**: This sets both `Values` and `Labels`, which triggers `CreateSubViews()` twice (once from `Values` setter, once from `Labels` setter). The first call creates subviews (since both are now set from the `Values` setter path), and the second call from `Labels` setter recreates them. The layout should be properly triggered both times.

6. **`SelectorStyles.ShowValue`**: Adds a `TextField` subview which doesn't have `PosAlign`. But the checkboxes still have `PosAlign`. The `TextField` won't be in the align group, so `CalculateMinDimension` won't include it. But the auto-width calculation should still account for it via other paths.

Let me verify with a quick test that includes ShowValue:







🎬 ACTION
cat > /testbed/ReproApp/Program2.cs << 'EOF'
using Terminal.Gui;
using Terminal.Gui.Views;
using Terminal.Gui.ViewBase;

// Test 1: Basic horizontal with ShowValue
var selector1 = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Horizontal,
    Styles = SelectorStyles.ShowValue,
};

selector1.Labels = ["IMDb (Recommended)", "TMDb"];
selector1.Values = [0, 1];

selector1.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("=== Test 1: Horizontal + ShowValue ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector1.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector1.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  CheckBox '{cb.Title}': Frame={cb.Frame}");
}
var valueField = selector1.SubViews.FirstOrDefault(v => v.Id == "valueField");
if (valueField != null)
    Console.WriteLine($"  ValueField: Frame={valueField.Frame}");

// Test 2: Vertical orientation
var selector2 = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Vertical,
};

selector2.Labels = ["Option 1", "Option 2", "Option 3"];
selector2.Values = [0, 1, 2];

selector2.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("\n=== Test 2: Vertical ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector2.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector2.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  CheckBox '{cb.Title}': Frame={cb.Frame}");
}

// Test 3: Changing labels after initial setup
var selector3 = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Horizontal,
};

selector3.Labels = ["Short", "Longer Label Here"];
selector3.Values = [0, 1];

selector3.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("\n=== Test 3: First layout ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector3.Frame}");

// Change labels
selector3.Labels = ["Very Very Long Label Here", "Short"];
selector3.Values = [0, 1];

selector3.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("\n=== Test 3: After label change ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector3.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector3.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  CheckBox '{cb.Title}': Frame={cb.Frame}");
}

// Test 4: Constructor then add to parent (simulating reactive binding)
var selector4 = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Horizontal,
};

// This simulates reactive binding: labels set after construction
selector4.Labels = ["Label A", "Label B", "Label C"];
selector4.Values = [1, 2, 3];

var parent = new View { Width = 100, Height = 10 };
parent.Add(selector4);
parent.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("\n=== Test 4: Added to parent after label setup ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector4.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector4.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  CheckBox '{cb.Title}': Frame={cb.Frame}");
}
EOF

using Terminal.Gui;
using Terminal.Gui.Views;
using Terminal.Gui.ViewBase;

// Test 1: Basic horizontal with ShowValue
var selector1 = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Horizontal,
    Styles = SelectorStyles.ShowValue,
};

selector1.Labels = ["IMDb (Recommended)", "TMDb"];
selector1.Values = [0, 1];

selector1.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("=== Test 1: Horizontal + ShowValue ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector1.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector1.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  CheckBox '{cb.Title}': Frame={cb.Frame}");
}
var valueField = selector1.SubViews.FirstOrDefault(v => v.Id == "valueField");
if (valueField != null)
    Console.WriteLine($"  ValueField: Frame={valueField.Frame}");

// Test 2: Vertical orientation
var selector2 = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Vertical,
};

selector2.Labels = ["Option 1", "Option 2", "Option 3"];
selector2.Values = [0, 1, 2];

selector2.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("\n=== Test 2: Vertical ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector2.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector2.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  CheckBox '{cb.Title}': Frame={cb.Frame}");
}

// Test 3: Changing labels after initial setup
var selector3 = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Horizontal,
};

selector3.Labels = ["Short", "Longer Label Here"];
selector3.Values = [0, 1];

selector3.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("\n=== Test 3: First layout ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector3.Frame}");

// Change labels
selector3.Labels = ["Very Very Long Label Here", "Short"];
selector3.Values = [0, 1];

selector3.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("\n=== Test 3: After label change ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector3.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector3.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  CheckBox '{cb.Title}': Frame={cb.Frame}");
}

// Test 4: Constructor then add to parent (simulating reactive binding)
var selector4 = new OptionSelector
{
    Orientation = Orientation.Horizontal,
};

selector4.Labels = ["Label A", "Label B", "Label C"];
selector4.Values = [1, 2, 3];

var parent = new View { Width = 100, Height = 10 };
parent.Add(selector4);
parent.Layout();

Console.WriteLine("\n=== Test 4: Added to parent after label setup ===");
Console.WriteLine($"Selector Frame: {selector4.Frame}");
foreach (var cb in selector4.SubViews.OfType<CheckBox>())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  CheckBox '{cb.Title}': Frame={cb.Frame}");
}
EOF

=== Final PosAlign.cs CalculateMinDimension ===

    // TODO: PosAlign.CalculateMinDimension is a hack. Need to figure out a better way of doing this.
    /// <summary>
    ///     Returns the minimum size a group of views with the same <paramref name="groupId"/> can be.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="groupId"></param>
    /// <param name="views"></param>
    /// <param name="dimension"></param>
    /// <returns></returns>
    public static int CalculateMinDimension (int groupId, IReadOnlyCollection<View> views, Dimension dimension)
    {
        var dimensionsSum = 0;

        foreach (View view in views)
        {
            if (!HasGroupId (view, dimension, groupId))
            {
                continue;
            }

            PosAlign? posAlign = dimension == Dimension.Width ? view.X as PosAlign : view.Y as PosAlign;

            if (posAlign is { })
            {
                dimensionsSum += dimension == Dimension.Width
                                     ? view.Width.Calculate (0, 0, view, dimension)
                                     : view.Height.Calculate (0, 0, view, dimension);
            }
        }

        // Align
